<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Friends_organisation">Friends organisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mount_Athos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Friends organisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Friends of Mount Athos (FoMA) is a society formed in 1990 by people who shared a common interest for the monasteries of Mount Athos. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timothy_Ware" title="Timothy Ware">Timothy Ware</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_bishop" title="Metropolitan bishop">Metropolitan</a> Kallistos of Diokleia, is the President and Chairman of the society. Among its members are <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Charles, Prince of Wales">Charles, Prince of Wales</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heir_Apparent" title="Heir Apparent">Heir Apparent</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_monarchy" title="British monarchy">British throne</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>The object of the society, as stated on its official web page, is officially described as: "the advancement of education of the public in the study and knowledge of the history, culture, arts, architecture, natural history, and literature of the Orthodox monasteries of Mount Athos and the promotion of the religious and other charitable work of the Holy Community and monasteries of Mount Athos." In keeping with those objects, the society is empowered "to make grants, donations and other payments for the restoration or conservation of buildings or of works of art and books of educational or religious significance on Mount Athos within the above objects." To that end the society produces publications, arranges lectures, and organizes conferences and exhibitions devoted to Athonite themes.</p>
<p>Among the society's publications are its annual bulletin (<i>Friends of Mount Athos Annual Report</i>) offering articles, book reviews and other features related to Mount Athos. It also publishes <i>A Pilgrim's Guide to Mount Athos</i> as well as a yearly directory of members.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mount_Athos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This tradition has been included by St Gregory Palamas into his book <i>"Life of Petros the Athonite"</i> p. 150, 1005AD.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">However, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Easter_date" title="Easter date">Easter date</a>, based on the lunar cycle, is still calculated following the original Julian calendar, making the Eastern Orthodox world celebrate Easter on the same day.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-45">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In accordance with Old Testament practice, the day is considered to begin in the evening (Genesis 1:5).</span></li>
</ol>
</div>

Panteleïmon is Russian, Simonopetra is Bulgarian, and Karakallou and Philotheou are Albanian. Zographou, Kastamonitou (see fig. 58), Xeropotamou, Koutloumousiou, Xenophontos, Iveron and Protaton he mentions without any designation; while Lavra, Vatopedi (see fig. 59), Pantokratoros, and Stavronikita (which had been recently founded by the patriarch Jeremiah I) he names specifically as being Greek (see map 6)</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMount+Athos&amp;rft.au=A.+E.+Bakalopulos&amp;rft.btitle=History+of+Macedonia%2C+1354%931833.+%26%2391%3BBy%26%2393%3B+A.E.+Vacalopoulos&amp;rft.date=1973&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DV5z_cQAACAAJ&amp;rft.pages=166-167&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-FRC-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FRC_26-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=7jIrAQAAIAAJ&amp;q=%22flag+of+Mount+Athos%22&amp;dq=%22flag+of+Mount+Athos%22&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ei=gZ-QVK2VN4q8yQT5h4HYDQ&amp;ved=0CCoQ6AEwAA" rel="nofollow"><i>The Flag Bulletin</i></a>. <b>27</b>. Flag Research Center. 1988. p. 105. <q>It is not surprising that all symbols of Mount Athos, especially the Byzantine double-headed eagle and the Holy Virgin, who is the patron of the Holy Mount, represent old Byzantine traditions. [...] The flag of Mount Athos (Fig. 1) is golden yellow bearing the black Byzantine double-headed eagle with an imperial crown. The eagle holds in its claws an orb of black with golden bands and a black sword. The flag is ... During the millennial celebration of Mount Athos, it was often possible to see this flag flying together with the national flag of Greece on top of the government buildings in Karyes.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMount+Athos&amp;rft.btitle=The+Flag+Bulletin&amp;rft.date=1988&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D7jIrAQAAIAAJ%26q%3D%2522flag%2Bof%2BMount%2BAthos%2522%26dq%3D%2522flag%2Bof%2BMount%2BAthos%2522%26hl%3Den%26sa%3DX%26ei%3DgZ-QVK2VN4q8yQT5h4HYDQ%26ved%3D0CCoQ6AEwAA&amp;rft.pages=105&amp;rft.pub=Flag+Research+Center.&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bibliography">Bibliography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mount_Athos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Bibliography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><i>The 6,000 Beards of Mount Athos</i> <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0859552519">ISBN 0-85955-251-9</a> by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ralph_H._Brewster&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ralph H. Brewster (page does not exist)">Ralph H. Brewster</a>. A guide to the peninsula, first published in 1935, detailing the landscape, monasteries, skites, and the life of the inhabitants, including customs and more not usually discussed.</li>
<li><i>Mount Athos</i> <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/960213075X">ISBN 960-213-075-X</a> by Sotiris Kadas. An illustrated guide to the monasteries and their history (Athens 1998). With many illustrations of the Byzantine art treasures on Mount Athos.</li>
<li><i>Athos The Holy Mountain</i> by Sydney Loch. Published 1957 &amp; 1971 (Librairie Molho, Thessaloniki). Loch spent most of his life in the Byzantine tower at Ouranopolis, close to Athos, and describes his numerous visits to the Holy Mountain. A fascinating travelogue. The famous Molho Bookstore in Thessaloniki may have a few copies left.</li>
<li><i>Dare to be Free</i> <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0330106295">ISBN 0-330-10629-5</a> by Walter Babington Thomas. Offers insights into the lives of the monks of Mt Athos during World War II, from the point of view of an escaped POW who spent a year on the peninsula evading capture.</li>
<li><i>Blue Guide: Greece</i> <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0393303721">ISBN 0-393-30372-1</a>, pp. 600–03. Offers history and tourist information.</li>
<li><i>Mount Athos: Renewal in Paradise</i> <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0300103239">ISBN 0-300-10323-9</a>, by Graham Speake. Published by Yale University Press in 2002. An extensive book about Athos in the past, the present and the future. Includes valuable tourist information. Features numerous full-colour photographs of the peninsula and daily life in the monasteries. Out of print.</li>
<li><i>From The Holy Mountain</i> by William Dalrymple. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0805061770">ISBN 0-8050-6177-0</a> Published 1997. A fascinating journey that begins from and constantly refers back to Mount Athos.</li>
<li><i>Mount Athos: Renewal in Paradise</i> by Graham Speake (Denise Harvey: Limni 2014), First Published by Yale University. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9789607120342">ISBN 978-960-7120-34-2</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>In this second edition of his acclaimed study of Mount Athos (for which he was awarded the 2002 Criticos Prize) the author takes the opportunity to revise and update his text and also to add a completely new chapter documenting the changes that have occurred in the twelve years since its first publication.</p>
<ul>
<li>Ivanov, Emil: <i>Das Bildprogramm des Narthex im Rila-Kloster in Bulgarien unter besonderer Berücksichtigung der Wasserweihezyklen auf dem Athos</i>, Diss., Erlangen, 2002.</li>
<li>Ivanov, Emil: Apokallypsedarstellungen in der nachbyzantinischen Kunst, in: Das Münster, 3, 2002, 208–217.</li>
<li><cite class="citation magazine">"Mount Athos". <i><a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_(magazine)" title="National Geographic (magazine)">National Geographic</a></i>. Vol. 164 no. 6. December 1983. pp. 738–766. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Serial_Number" title="International Standard Serial Number">ISSN</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/issn/0027-9358" rel="nofollow">0027-9358</a>. <a href="/wiki/OCLC" title="OCLC">OCLC</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/oclc/643483454" rel="nofollow">643483454</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMount+Athos&amp;rft.btitle=Mount+Athos&amp;rft.date=1983-12&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=info%3Aoclcnum%2F643483454&amp;rft.issn=0027-9358&amp;rft.pages=738-766&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></li>
</ul>
